MSA">Virginia Beach-Norfolk-Newport News, VA-NC MSA</a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr class="mergedrow">\n<th scope="row">Largest city</th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a></td>\n</tr>\n<tr class="mergedtoprow">\n<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align:left">Area</th>\n</tr>\n<tr class="mergedrow">\n<th scope="row">\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\xa2\xc2\xa0Total</th>\n<td>191,308.5\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi (495,487\xc2\xa0km<sup>2</sup>)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr class="mergedtoprow">\n<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align:left">Population <span style="font-weight:normal">(2008 est.)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></span></th>\n</tr>\n<tr class="mergedrow">\n<th scope="row">\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\xa2\xc2\xa0Total</th>\n<td>57,303,316</td>\n</tr>\n<tr class="mergedrow">\n<th scope="row">\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\xa2\xc2\xa0Density</th>\n<td>300/sq\xc2\xa0mi (120/km<sup>2</sup>)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr class="mergedtoprow">\n<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align:left"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GDP" title="GDP">GDP</a><span style="font-weight:normal"><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></span></th>\n</tr>\n<tr class="mergedrow">\n<th scope="row">\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\xa2\xc2\xa0Total</th>\n<td>$2.962 trillion (2007)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>The <b>Mid-Atlantic</b>, also called <b>Middle Atlantic states</b> or the <b>Mid-Atlantic states</b>, form a region of the United States generally located between <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> and the <a href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_States" title="South Atlantic States">South Atlantic States</a>. Its exact definition differs upon source, but the region usually includes <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia" title="West Virginia">West Virginia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> The Mid-Atlantic has played an important role in the development of American <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_culture" title="American culture">culture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commerce" title="Commerce">commerce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trade" title="Trade">trade</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Industry" title="Industry">industry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In the late 19th century, it was called "the typically American" region by <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Jackson_Turner" title="Frederick Jackson Turner">Frederick Jackson Turner</a>. Religious pluralism and ethnic diversity have been important elements of Mid-Atlantic society from its settlement by <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swedish_people" title="Swedish people">Swedes</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_England_and_Wales" title="Roman Catholicism in England and Wales">English Catholics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Quakers" title="Quakers">Quakers</a> through to the period of English rule, and beyond to the current day. After the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>, the Mid-Atlantic region hosted each of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_capitals_in_the_United_States" title="List of capitals in the United States">historic capitals of the United States</a>, including the current federal capital, <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a></p>\n<p>In the early part of the 19th century, <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a> overtook <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a> as the most populous states and the <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> states as the country\'s most important trading and industrial centers. Large numbers of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_American" title="German American">German</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_American" title="Irish American">Irish</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_American" title="Italian American">Italian</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_American" title="Jewish American">Jewish</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish_American" title="Polish American">Polish</a>, and other <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Immigration to the United States">immigrants</a> transformed the region, especially coastal cities such as <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newark,_New_Jersey" title="Newark, New Jersey">Newark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, but also interior cities such as <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albany,_New_York" title="Albany, New York">Albany</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Buffalo,_New_York" title="Buffalo, New York">Buffalo</a>.</p>\n<p>New York City, with its skyscrapers, subways, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Headquarters" title="United Nations Headquarters">headquarters of the United Nations</a>, emerged in the 20th century as an icon of <a href="/wiki/Modernity" title="Modernity">modernity</a> and American economic and cultural power. By the 21st century, the coastal areas of the Mid-Atlantic were thoroughly urbanized.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Corridor" title="Northeast Corridor">Northeast Corridor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95" title="Interstate 95">Interstate 95</a> link an almost contiguous <a href="/wiki/Urban_sprawl" title="Urban sprawl">sprawl</a> of <a href="/wiki/Suburb" title="Suburb">suburbs</a> and large and small cities, forming the Mid-Atlantic portion of the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_megalopolis" title="Northeast megalopolis">Northeast megalopolis</a>, one of the world\'s most important concentrations of <a href="/wiki/Finance" title="Finance">finance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Media_(communication)" title="Media (communication)">media</a>, communications, <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">education</a>, medicine, and technology.</p>\n<p>The Mid-Atlantic is a relatively affluent region of the nation, having 43 of the 100 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Highest-income_counties_in_the_United_States" title="Highest-income counties in the United States">highest-income counties</a> in the nation based on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Median_household_income" title="Median household income">median household income</a> and 33 of the top 100 based on <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">per capita income</a>. Most of the Mid-Atlantic states rank among the 15 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/States_of_the_United_States_of_America_by_income" title="States of the United States of America by income">highest-income states</a> in the nation by median household income and per capita income.</p>\n<p></p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc">\n<div class="toctitle">\n<h2>Contents</h2>\n</div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<p></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Defining_the_Mid-Atlantic">Defining the Mid-Atlantic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mid-Atlantic_states&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Defining the Mid-Atlantic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mid-Atlantic_Region_location_map.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="357" data-file-width="210" height="306" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Mid-Atlantic_Region_location_map.gif/180px-Mid-Atlantic_Region_location_map.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4f/Mid-Atlantic_Region_location_map.gif 1.5x" width="180"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mid-Atlantic_Region_location_map.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA <a href="/wiki/United_States_Geological_Survey" title="United States Geological Survey">USGS</a> Fact Sheet interpretation of the Mid-Atlantic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Middle_Atlantic_States_-_1883_Monteith_map.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1472" data-file-width="1184" height="311" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Middle_Atlantic_States_-_1883_Monteith_map.jpg/250px-Middle_Atlantic_States_-_1883_Monteith_map.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Middle_Atlantic_States_-_1883_Monteith_map.jpg/375px-Middle_Atlantic_States_-_1883_Monteith_map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Middle_Atlantic_States_-_1883_Monteith_map.jpg/500px-Middle_Atlantic_States_-_1883_Monteith_map.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Middle_Atlantic_States_-_1883_Monteith_map.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nAn 1897 map displays an inclusive definition of the Mid-Atlantic region.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>There are differing interpretations as to the composition of the Mid-Atlantic, and has at times included any state from New York to South Carolina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Most commonly included is the Mid-Atlantic states as defined by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Census_Bureau" title="Census Bureau">Census Bureau</a>--<a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>\xe2\x80\x94along with the <a href="/wiki/Border_states_(American_Civil_War)" title="Border states (American Civil War)">Civil War border states</a> of <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, and <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia" title="West Virginia">West Virginia</a>. Sometimes, the nucleus is considered to be the area centered on the <a href="/wiki/Washington_metropolitan_area" title="Washington metropolitan area">Washington metropolitan area</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a>, and <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia" title="West Virginia">West Virginia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Since the <a href="/wiki/1910_United_States_Census" title="1910 United States Census">1910 census</a>, the Mid-Atlantic Census Division has included New Jersey, New York, and Pennsylvania, which combined with the <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England Division</a>, comprised the <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">Northeast Census Region</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-census-9">[9]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/United_States_Geological_Survey" title="United States Geological Survey">United States Geological Survey</a> publication describes the Mid-Atlantic Region as all of Maryland, Delaware, Pennsylvania, and Virginia, along with the parts of New Jersey, New York, and <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a> that <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">drain into</a> the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Bay" title="Delaware Bay">Delaware</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">Chesapeake Bays</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Albemarle_Sound" title="Albemarle Sound">Albemarle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pamlico_Sound" title="Pamlico Sound">Pamlico Sounds</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>\n<p>West Virginia and Virginia are atypical of this region in several ways. They are the only states to lie primarily within the <a href="/wiki/Southern_American_English" title="Southern American English">Southern American dialect region</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> and the major religious tradition in both states is Evangelical Christian, 31% in Virginia and 36% in West Virginia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Although a few of West Virginia\'s eastern panhandle counties are considered part of the <a href="/wiki/Washington_metropolitan_area" title="Washington metropolitan area">Washington, D.C. MSA</a>, the major portion of the state is rural, and there are no major or even large cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span id=\'The_"typically_American"_region\'></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_.22typically_American.22_region">The "typically American" region</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mid-Atlantic_states&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title=\'Edit section: The "typically American" region\'>edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>wrote in 1893 about the important role the Mid-Atlantic or "Middle region" had played in the formation of the national American culture, and defined it as "the typical American region".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>\n<table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">\n<tr>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: \'Times New Roman\', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9c</td>\n<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">The Middle region, entered by <a href="/wiki/New_York_Harbor" title="New York Harbor">New York harbor</a>, was an open door to all Europe. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tidewater_region_of_Virginia" title="Tidewater region of Virginia">tide-water</a> part of the South represented typical Englishmen, modified by a warm climate and servile labor, and living in baronial fashion on great plantations; New England stood for a special English movement-- <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puritan" title="Puritan">Puritanism</a>. The Middle region was less English than the other sections. It had a wide mixture of nationalities, a varied society, the mixed town and county system of local government, a varied economic life, many religious sects. In short, it was a region mediating between New England and the South, and the East and the West. It represented that composite nationality which the contemporary United States exhibits, that juxtaposition of non-English groups, occupying a valley or a little settlement, and presenting reflections of the map of Europe in their variety. It was democratic and nonsectional, if not national; "easy, tolerant, and contented;" rooted strongly in material prosperity. It was typical of the modern United States. It was least sectional, not only because it lay between North and South, but also because with no barriers to shut out its frontiers from its settled region, and with a system of connecting waterways, the Middle region mediated between East and West as well as between North and South. Thus it became the typically American region. Even the New Englander, who was shut out from the frontier by the Middle region, tarrying in New York or Pennsylvania on his westward march, lost the acuteness of his sectionalism on the way.</td>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: \'Times New Roman\', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9d</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td class="cquotecite" colspan="3" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; text-align: right;"><cite>\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x89<i>The Frontier in American History</i></cite></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mid-Atlantic_states&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Line3174_-_Shipping_Containers_at_the_terminal_at_Port_Elizabeth,_New_Jersey_-_NOAA.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1632" data-file-width="2448" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Line3174_-_Shipping_Containers_at_the_terminal_at_Port_Elizabeth%2C_New_Jersey_-_NOAA.jpg/300px-Line3174_-_Shipping_Containers_at_the_terminal_at_Port_Elizabeth%2C_New_Jersey_-_NOAA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Line3174_-_Shipping_Containers_at_the_terminal_at_Port_Elizabeth%2C_New_Jersey_-_NOAA.jpg/450px-Line3174_-_Shipping_Containers_at_the_terminal_at_Port_Elizabeth%2C_New_Jersey_-_NOAA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Line3174_-_Shipping_Containers_at_the_terminal_at_Port_Elizabeth%2C_New_Jersey_-_NOAA.jpg/600px-Line3174_-_Shipping_Containers_at_the_terminal_at_Port_Elizabeth%2C_New_Jersey_-_NOAA.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Line3174_-_Shipping_Containers_at_the_terminal_at_Port_Elizabeth,_New_Jersey_-_NOAA.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Intermodal_container" title="Intermodal container">Shipping containers</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Port_Newark-Elizabeth_Marine_Terminal" title="Port Newark-Elizabeth Marine Terminal">Port Newark-Elizabeth Marine Terminal</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_New_York_and_New_Jersey" title="Port of New York and New Jersey">Port of New York and New Jersey</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Shipping and trade have been important to the Mid-Atlantic economy since the beginning of the colonial era.</p>\n<p>The explorer <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_da_Verrazzano" title="Giovanni da Verrazzano">Giovanni da Verrazzano</a> was the first European to see the region in 1524. <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hudson" title="Henry Hudson">Henry Hudson</a> later extensively explored that region in 1609 and claimed it for the Dutch, who then created a fur-trading post in <a href="/wiki/Albany,_New_York" title="Albany, New York">Albany</a> in 1614. <a href="/wiki/Jamestown,_Virginia" title="Jamestown, Virginia">Jamestown, Virginia</a> was the first permanent English colony in North America seven years earlier in 1607.</p>\n<p>From early colonial times, the Mid-Atlantic region was settled by a wider range of European people than in New England or the South. The Dutch <a href="/wiki/New_Netherland" title="New Netherland">New Netherland</a> settlement along the Hudson River in New York and New Jersey, and for a time, <a href="/wiki/New_Sweden" title="New Sweden">New Sweden</a> along the Delaware River in Delaware, divided the two great bulwarks of English settlement from each other. The original English settlements in the region notably provided refuge to religious minorities, Maryland to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholics</a>, and Pennsylvania to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Religious_Society_of_Friends" title="Religious Society of Friends">Quakers</a> and the mostly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anabaptist" title="Anabaptist">Anabaptist</a> <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Dutch" title="Pennsylvania Dutch">Pennsylvania Dutch</a>. In time, all these settlements fell under English colonial control, but the region continued to be a magnet for people of diverse nationalities.</p>\n<p>The area that came to be known as the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Colonies" title="Middle Colonies">Middle Colonies</a> served as a strategic bridge between the North and South. The <a href="/wiki/New_York_and_New_Jersey_campaign" title="New York and New Jersey campaign">New York and New Jersey campaign</a> during the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a> saw more battles than any other theater of the conflict. <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, midway between the northern and southern colonies, was home to the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Congress" title="Continental Congress">Continental Congress</a>, the convention of delegates who organized the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>. The same city was the birthplace of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">Declaration of Independence</a> in 1776 and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">United States Constitution</a> in 1787, while the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Bill_of_Rights" title="United States Bill of Rights">United States Bill of Rights</a> was drafted and ratified, and the first <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court of the United States</a> sat for the first time, in the first capital under the Constitution at New York City.</p>\n<p>While early settlers were mostly farmers, traders, and fishermen, the Mid-Atlantic states provided the young United States with <a href="/wiki/Heavy_industry" title="Heavy industry">heavy industry</a> and served as the "<a href="/wiki/Melting_pot" title="Melting pot">melting pot</a>" of new <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Immigration to the United States">immigrants</a> from Europe. Cities grew along major ports, shipping routes, and waterways. Such flourishing cities included New York City and <a href="/wiki/Newark,_New_Jersey" title="Newark, New Jersey">Newark</a> on opposite sides of the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">Hudson River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River" title="Delaware River">Delaware River</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">Chesapeake Bay</a>.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_cities_and_urban_areas">Major cities and urban areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mid-Atlantic_states&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Major cities and urban areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div Virginia</a></li>\n</ul>\n<p>Note: The Mid-Atlantic region is also home to the nation\'s capital, <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mid-Atlantic_states&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mid-Atlantic_states&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Mid-Atlantic is home to several professional sports franchises in <a href="/wiki/Major_professional_sports_leagues_in_the_United_States_and_Canada" title="Major professional sports leagues in the United States and Canada">major leagues</a>:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>New York metropolitan area: <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">Giants</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_Jets" title="New York Jets">Jets</a> (NFL), <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">Yankees</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">Mets</a> (MLB), <a href="/wiki/New_York_Knicks" title="New York Knicks">Knicks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Nets" title="Brooklyn Nets">Nets</a> (NBA), <a href="/wiki/New_York_Rangers" title="New York Rangers">Rangers</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_Islanders" title="New York Islanders">Islanders</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Devils" title="New Jersey Devils">Devils</a> (NHL)</li>\n<li>Philadelphia: <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Eagles" title="Philadelphia Eagles">Eagles</a> (NFL), <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Phillies</a> (MLB), <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_76ers" title="Philadelphia 76ers">76ers</a> (NBA), <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Flyers" title="Philadelphia Flyers">Flyers</a> (NHL)</li>\n<li>Washington, D.C.: <a href="/wiki/Washington_Redskins" title="Washington Redskins">Redskins</a> (NFL), <a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">Nationals</a> (MLB), <a href="/wiki/Washington_Wizards" title="Washington Wizards">Wizards</a> (NBA), <a href="/wiki/Washington_Capitals" title="Washington Capitals">Capitals</a> (NHL)</li>\n<li>Baltimore: <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Ravens" title="Baltimore Ravens">Ravens</a> (NFL), <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Orioles</a> (MLB)</li>\n<li>Pittsburgh: <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Steelers" title="Pittsburgh Steelers">Steelers</a> (NFL), <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">Pirates</a> (MLB), <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Penguins" title="Pittsburgh Penguins">Penguins</a> (NHL)</li>\n<li>Buffalo: <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Bills" title="Buffalo Bills">Bills</a> (NFL), <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Sabres" title="Buffalo Sabres">Sabres</a> (NHL)</li>\n</ul>\n<p>In addition, the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a> features four Mid-Atlantic teams: <a href="/wiki/D.C._United" title="D.C. United">D.C. United</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_FC" title="New York City FC">New York City FC</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_Red_Bulls" title="New York Red Bulls">New York Red Bulls</a> and <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Union" title="Philadelphia Union">Philadelphia Union</a>, as well as two <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_National_Basketball_Association" title="Women\'s National Basketball Association">WNBA</a> teams: <a href="/wiki/New_York_Liberty" title="New York Liberty">New York Liberty</a> and <a href="/wiki/Washington_Mystics" title="Washington Mystics">Washington Mystics</a>.</p>\n<p>Notable golf tournaments in the Mid-Atlantic include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Barclays" title="The Barclays">Barclays</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quicken_Loans_National" title="Quicken Loans National">Quicken Loans National</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic_City_LPGA_Classic" title="Atlantic City LPGA Classic">Atlantic City LPGA Classic</a>. The <a href="/wiki/US_Open_(tennis)" title="US Open (tennis)">US Open</a>, held at New York City, is one of the four Grand Slam tennis tournaments, whereas <a href="/wiki/Washington_Open_(tennis)" title="Washington Open (tennis)">Washington Open</a> is part of the <a href="/wiki/ATP_World_Tour_500_series" title="ATP World Tour 500 series">ATP World Tour 500 series</a>.</p>\n<p>Notable motorsports tracks include <a href="/wiki/Watkins_Glen_International" title="Watkins Glen International">Watkins Glen International</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dover_International_Speedway" title="Dover International Speedway">Dover International Speedway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pocono_Raceway" title="Pocono Raceway">Pocono Raceway</a>, which have hosted <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IndyCar" title="IndyCar">IndyCar</a>, <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Sportscar_Championship" title="World Sportscar Championship">World Sportscar Championship</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_Motor_Sports_Association" title="International Motor Sports Association">IMSA</a> races. Also, the <a href="/wiki/Old_Bridge_Township_Raceway_Park" title="Old Bridge Township Raceway Park">Englishtown</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maple_Grove_Raceway" title="Maple Grove Raceway">Reading</a> drag strips such have hosted <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NHRA" title="NHRA">NHRA</a> national events. <a href="/wiki/Pimlico_Race_Course" title="Pimlico Race Course">Pimlico Race Course</a> at Baltimore and <a href="/wiki/Belmont_Park" title="Belmont Park">Belmont Park</a> at New York host the <a href="/wiki/Preakness_Stakes" title="Preakness Stakes">Preakness Stakes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belmont_Stakes" title="Belmont Stakes">Belmont Stakes</a> horse races, which are part of the <a href="/wiki/Triple_Crown_of_Thoroughbred_Racing_(United_States)" title="Triple Crown of Thoroughbred Racing (United States)">Triple Crown of Thoroughbred Racing</a>.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mid-Atlantic_states&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_regions_of_the_United_States" title="List of regions of the United States">List of regions of the United States</a></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
